10.1016/j.jmp.2021.102564
In the theory of knowledge structures, a number of one-to-one correspondences were established between particular collections of mathematical structures. Let  
                         Q 
                       be a nonempty set and  
                         P 
                       be a relation on  
                         Q 
                      . Recall that the pair  
                         
                            ( 
                            Q 
                            , 
                            P 
                            ) 
                         
                       is a quasi ordered set, or equivalently,  
                         P 
                       is a quasi order on  
                         Q 
                      , if and only if  
                         P 
                       is reflexive and transitive. As a celebrated result,  Birkhoff (1937)  confirmed the existence of a one-to-one correspondence between the collection of all quasi ordinal spaces on  
                         Q 
                       and the collection of all quasi orders on  
                         Q 
                      . It was known that this correspondence derived from natural constructions and the derivation is obtained from the application of a general result about “Galois connections” (see, e.g.  Falmagne & Doignon, 2011 ). In the past years, some Galois connections were established. For example,  Doignon and Falmagne (1985)  established a Galois connection between the collection of all knowledge structures on a finite domain  
                         Q 
                       and the collection of all attribution functions on  
                         Q 
                      . In addition, a compendium of the notation for the various collections and the three Galois connections of main interest was given in  Falmagne and Doignon (2011) . Here, the definition of Galois connections was introduced by  Doignon and Falmagne (1985) , which involves a slight generalization of a standard concept ( Birkhoff, 1967 ).

In order to give the Galois connection of  Doignon and Falmagne (1985) , we need some definitions about attribution functions and knowledge structures.

Attribution functions and surmise functions were introduced by  Doignon and Falmagne (1985) , where they were called “surmise mapping” and “space-like surmise mapping” respectively. This paper describes attribution functions and surmise functions in the sense of  Falmagne and Doignon (2011) . Throughout this paper, the family of all subsets of a set  
                         Q 
                      , or power set of  
                         Q 
                      , is symbolized by  
                         
                            
                               2 
                            
                            
                               Q 
                            
                         
                      .

As a traditional explanatory feature of mathematical psychology theory, the attribution function is consistent with the following knowledge space (e.g., see  Doignon & Falmagne, 1999; Falmagne et al. (Eds.), 2013; Falmagne & Doignon, 2011; Spoto et al., 2013 ). In Doignon and Falmagne’s early papers ( Doignon & Falmagne, 1985, 1988 ), a knowledge structure need not contain the domain and the empty set. In this paper, we adopt the knowledge structure in the sense of  Doignon and Falmagne (1999) .

Definition 3 
                         
                            Doignon & Falmagne, 1999 
                         
                         A knowledge structure is a pair  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  K 
                                  ) 
                               
                             in which  
                               Q 
                             is a nonempty set, and  
                               K 
                             is a family of subsets of  
                               Q 
                            , containing at least  
                               Q 
                             and the empty set  
                               0̸ 
                            . We also often say that  
                               K 
                             is a knowledge structure on a set  
                               Q 
                             to mean that  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  K 
                                  ) 
                               
                             is a knowledge structure. The set  
                               Q 
                             is called the domain of the knowledge structure. Its elements are referred to as questions or items and the subsets in the family  
                               K 
                             are labeled (knowledge) states. Further, the knowledge structure  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  K 
                                  ) 
                               
                             is called a knowledge space if the family  
                               K 
                             is union-closed. Here, a family  
                               U 
                             of sets is called union-closed if  
                               
                                  ⋃ 
                                  ℱ 
                                  ∈ 
                                  U 
                               
                             whenever  
                               
                                  ℱ 
                                  ⊆ 
                                  U 
                               
                            .

A knowledge structure is a pair  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  K 
                                  ) 
                               
                             in which  
                               Q 
                             is a nonempty set, and  
                               K 
                             is a family of subsets of  
                               Q 
                            , containing at least  
                               Q 
                             and the empty set  
                               0̸ 
                            . We also often say that  
                               K 
                             is a knowledge structure on a set  
                               Q 
                             to mean that  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  K 
                                  ) 
                               
                             is a knowledge structure. The set  
                               Q 
                             is called the domain of the knowledge structure. Its elements are referred to as questions or items and the subsets in the family  
                               K 
                             are labeled (knowledge) states. Further, the knowledge structure  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  Q 
                                  , 
                                  K 
                                  ) 
                               
                             is called a knowledge space if the family  
                               K 
                             is union-closed. Here, a family  
                               U 
                             of sets is called union-closed if  
                               
                                  ⋃ 
                                  ℱ 
                                  ∈ 
                                  U 
                               
                             whenever  
                               
                                  ℱ 
                                  ⊆ 
                                  U 
                               
                            .

Recall that a quasi ordered set  
                         
                            ( 
                            X 
                            , 
                            S 
                            ) 
                         
                       is a partially ordered set if and only if  
                         S 
                       is antisymmetric on  
                         X 
                      . In such a case, we also say that  
                         S 
                       is a partial order on  
                         X 
                      
 (cf. e.g.  Roberts, 1979 ). Let  
                         K 
                       denote the collection of all knowledge structures on a domain  
                         Q 
                      . Then  
                         
                            ( 
                            K 
                            , 
                            ⊆ 
                            ) 
                         
                       is a partially ordered set. However,  
                         
                            ( 
                            F 
                            , 
                            ≾ 
                            ) 
                         
                       need not be a partially ordered set in general.

Two links between attribution functions and knowledge spaces were established by  Doignon and Falmagne (1985)  for the finite domain.

                            Doignon & Falmagne, 1985

                                  { 
                                  K 
                                  ∈ 
                                  K 
                                  ∣ 
                                  q 
                                  ∈ 
                                  K 
                                  } 
                               
                             
                            and  
                            
                               
                                  
                                     K 
                                     
                                        ( 
                                        q 
                                        ) 
                                     
                                  
                                  
                                     ̂ 
                                  
                               
                             
                            denotes the set of all minimal states (with respect to set inclusion) of  
                            
                               
                                  K 
                                  
                                     ( 
                                     q 
                                     ) 
                                  
                               
                            
                            . Put  
                            
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        σ 
                                     
                                     
                                        K 
                                     
                                  
                                  
                                     ( 
                                     q

Taking  Proposition 1  into account, a more general perspective should be taken, that avoids restricting the domain  
                         Q 
                       to being finite when establishing Galois connections. It is known that the mappings  
                         
                            f

                            K 
                         
                       if the domain  
                         Q 
                       is not finite (refer to Example 3.4(1) of  Doignon & Falmagne, 1985 ). This leads us to consider the following question.

Question 1 
                         
                            Is there a general way to derive an attribution function from a knowledge structure on an arbitrary domain?

Is there a general way to derive an attribution function from a knowledge structure on an arbitrary domain?

Further, if the answer of  Question 1  is positive, then the following question arises naturally.

In the discussion of  Questions 1 and 2 , it is useful to introduce the granularity of knowledge structures and attribution functions for arbitrary domains.

Definition 5 
                         
                            Falmagne & Doignon, 2011 
                         
                         
                            An attribution function is granular if the knowledge space it produces is granular.

An attribution function is granular if the knowledge space it produces is granular.

By the granularity,  Falmagne and Doignon (2011)  gave a way for deriving a granular attribution function from a granular knowledge structure on an arbitrary domain. Let  
                         
                            
                               K 
                            
                            
                               g 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            
                               F 
                            
                            
                               g 
                            
                         
                       denote the collection of all granular knowledge structures on an arbitrary domain  
                         Q 
                       and the collection of all granular attribution functions on  
                         Q 
                      , respectively. With the help of the above way,  Falmagne and Doignon (2011)  established a Galois connection between  
                         
                            ( 
                            
                               
                                  K 
                               
                               
                                  g 
                               
                            
                            , 
                            ⊆ 
                            ) 
                         
                       and  
                         
                            ( 
                            
                               
                                  F 
                               
                               
                                  g 
                               
                            
                            , 
                            ≾ 
                            ) 
                         
                      . These results give some partial answers to  Questions 1 and 2 . However, it is still open whether the granularity can be omitted here. This makes it interesting to solve  Questions 1 and 2  thoroughly. Further, there still remains a question on the granularity of attribution functions, which is dealt with Galois connections.

Definition 5  shows that the granularity of attribution functions is defined by the property that such an attribution function produces a granular knowledge space. It is known that every finite knowledge space is granular. It follows that every attribution function on a finite domain is granular. However, a direct characterization for granular attribution functions on infinite domains has not been proposed yet. This brings about the discussion for the granularity of attribution functions without requiring finite domains. In view of all this, the following question was posed by Falmagne and Doignon (see Open Problem 18.3.2 in  Falmagne & Doignon, 2011 ).

Question 3 
                         
                            Falmagne & Doignon, 2011 
                         
                         
                            What is a direct characterization of granular attribution functions?

What is a direct characterization of granular attribution functions?

Up to now,  Questions 1–3  are still open and we have not yet found related reports on the research progress in these topics. Our discussion spreads around these questions and the main aims of this paper are to solve these questions thoroughly.

Throughout this paper, the domain of an attribution function is some nonempty set  
                         Q 
                       by default if not mentioned otherwise, where  
                         Q 
                       need not be finite. In addition, we also use the following notations in this paper.

Notation 1 
                         (1)  
                               
                                  ( 
                                  K 
                                  , 
                                  ⊆ 
                                  ) 
                               
                             is a partially ordered set, where  
                               K 
                             is the collection of all knowledge structures on a domain  
                               Q 
                             and  
                               ⊆ 
                             is the relation of set inclusion.

(1)

(2)

                         ≾

                         ≾

                         F 
                       described after  Definition 2 .

In his paper,  Shen (2008)  introduced completeness for generalized neighborhood systems. Inspired by this, we generalize completeness from generalized neighborhood systems to attribution functions.

                         ≈

By  Proposition 2 , we have the existence and uniqueness theorem for the completion of attribution functions.

Theorem 1 
                         
                            Every attribution function has a unique completion.

Every attribution function has a unique completion.

Corollary 1 
                         
                            An attribution function is complete if and only if it equals its completion.

An attribution function is complete if and only if it equals its completion.

As an affirmative answer to  Question 1 , the following proposition gives a general way to derive an attribution function from a knowledge structure on an arbitrary domain. Idea of this way is distinctive and innovative though the proof of  Proposition 3  is straightforward (we omit the proof).

It is known that the dual knowledge structure of every knowledge structure is a knowledge space (see  Lemma 2 ). So a knowledge structure need not equal its dual knowledge structure. In the following, we give a necessary and sufficient condition such that a knowledge structure equals its dual knowledge structure.

Likewise, an attribution function need not equal its dual attribution function. In fact, let  
                         
                            Q 
                            = 
                            
                               { 
                               p 
                               , 
                               q 
                               } 
                            
                         
                       and let an attribution function  
                         σ 
                       on  
                         Q 
                       be defined as follows:  
                         
                            σ 
                            
                               ( 
                               p 
                               ) 
                            
                            = 
                            
                               { 
                               
                                  { 
                                  p 
                                  } 
                               
                               } 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            σ 
                            
                               ( 
                               q 
                               ) 
                            
                            = 
                            
                               { 
                               
                                  { 
                                  q 
                                  } 
                               
                               } 
                            
                         
                      . Then  
                         
                            
                               
                                  K 
                               
                               
                                  σ 
                               
                            
                            = 
                            
                               { 
                               0̸ 
                               , 
                               
                                  { 
                                  p 
                                  } 
                               
                               , 
                               
                                  { 
                                  q 
                                  } 
                               
                               , 
                               Q 
                               } 
                            
                         
                      . It follows that  
                         
                            
                               
                                  σ 
                               
                               
                                  ∗ 
                               
                            
                            
                               ( 
                               p 
                               ) 
                            
                            = 
                            
                               { 
                               
                                  { 
                                  p 
                                  } 
                               
                               , 
                               Q 
                               } 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            
                               
                                  σ 
                               
                               
                                  ∗ 
                               
                            
                            
                               ( 
                               q 
                               ) 
                            
                            = 
                            
                               { 
                               
                                  { 
                                  q 
                                  } 
                               
                               , 
                               Q 
                               } 
                            
                         
                      . This shows that  
                         
                            σ 
                            ≠ 
                            
                               
                                  σ 
                               
                               
                                  ∗ 
                               
                            
                         
                      . By the completeness of attribution functions, we give some necessary and sufficient conditions such that an attribution function equals its dual attribution function.

By the above, a characterization of the completion of attribution functions can be obtained easily.

Proposition 7 
                         
                            Let  
                            
                               σ 
                             
                            be an attribution function on a domain  
                            
                               Q 
                            
                            . Then an attribution function  
                            
                               ρ

The following example comes from Remarks 3.4 of  Doignon and Falmagne (1985) , which shows that

                               Q

                                  =

                                  ≈

In decision system theory, the reduct of attributes was introduced for incomplete information systems (e.g., see  Wu, 2008 ). Here, attributes in decision system theory are different from attribution functions in knowledge space theory. In decision system theory, if  
                         
                            A 
                            T 
                         
                       denotes the set of all attributes in some incomplete information system, then the reduct of attributes is a minimal subset  
                         
                            A 
                            ⊆ 
                            A 
                            T 
                         
                       such that  
                         A 
                       and  
                         
                            A 
                            T 
                         
                       determine the same similarity relation. Inspired by these, we introduce the reduct of attribution functions in knowledge space theory to characterize the granularity of attribution functions.

Definition 8 
                         Let  
                               σ 
                             be an attribution function on a domain  
                               Q 
                            .  
                               
                                  
                                     σ 
                                  
                                  
                                     ̂ 
                                  
                               
                             is called the reduct of  
                               σ 
                             if  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        σ 
                                     
                                     
                                        ̂ 
                                     
                                  
                                  ≾ 
                                  σ 
                               
                             (equivalently,  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        σ 
                                     
                                     
                                        ̂ 
                                     
                                  
                                  ≈ 
                                  σ 
                               
                            ). Meanwhile we also say that  
                               σ 
                             has a reduct.

Let  
                               σ 
                             be an attribution function on a domain  
                               Q 
                            .  
                               
                                  
                                     σ 
                                  
                                  
                                     ̂ 
                                  
                               
                             is called the reduct of  
                               σ 
                             if  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        σ 
                                     
                                     
                                        ̂ 
                                     
                                  
                                  ≾ 
                                  σ 
                               
                             (equivalently,  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        σ 
                                     
                                     
                                        ̂ 
                                     
                                  
                                  ≈ 
                                  σ 
                               
                            ). Meanwhile we also say that  
                               σ 
                             has a reduct.

Clearly, for any attribution function  
                         σ 
                       on a finite domain,  
                         σ 
                       has a reduct because  
                         
                            
                               
                                  σ 
                               
                               
                                  ̂ 
                               
                            
                            ≈ 
                            σ 
                         
                       (see  Remark 1 (4)).

Lemma 11 
                         
                            Let  
                            
                               σ 
                             
                            be an attribution function on a domain  
                            
                               Q 
                            
                            . If  
                            
                               
                                  
                                     σ 
                                  
                                  
                                     ⋇ 
                                  
                               
                             
                            has a reduct, then  
                            
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        K

The following theorem gives a direct characterization of granular attribution functions without dealing with the derived knowledge spaces, which answers  Question 3  affirmatively.

Theorem 3 
                         
                            Let  
                            
                               σ 
                             
                            be an attribution function on a domain  
                            
                               Q 
                            
                            . Then the following are equivalent. 
                         
                         
                            (1)  
                            
                               σ 
                             
                            is granular. 
                         
                         
                            (2)  
                            
                               
                                  
                                     σ 
                                  
                                  
                                     ⋇ 
                                  
                               
                             
                            has a reduct.

Remark 2

In Section  3 , it is shown that there is a one-to-onecorrespondence between knowledge spaces and complete attribution functions. Moreover, this bijection induces a one-to-one correspondence between

Let  
                         σ 
                       be a complete attribution function on a domain  
                         Q 
                      . Then  
                         
                            σ 
                            = 
                            
                               
                                  σ 
                               
                               
                                  ⋇ 
                               
                            
                         
                       (see  Corollary 1 ). So  
                         
                            
                               σ 
                            
                            
                               ⋇ 
                            
                         
                       has a reduct if and only if  
                         σ 
                       has a reduct. Thus, the following corollary is obtained from  Theorem 3  immediately.

Corollary 3 
                         
                            A complete attribution function  
                            
                               σ 
                             
                            is granular if and only if  
                            
                               σ 
                             
                            has a reduct.

A complete attribution function  
                            
                               σ 
                             
                            is granular if and only if  
                            
                               σ 
                             
                            has a reduct.

The following two examples show that “ 
                         
                            
                               σ 
                            
                            
                               ⋇ 
                            
                         
                      ” in  Theorem 3 (2) cannot be replaced with “ 
                         σ 
                      ”. Here, one shows that a granular attribution function  
                         σ 
                       need not have a reduct, the other shows that an attribution function  
                         σ 
                       having a reduct need not be granular. Meanwhile, the two examples also show that “complete” in  Corollary 3  cannot be omitted.

Proposition 8 
                         
                            Falmagne & Doignon, 2011 
                         
                         
                            Every surmise function on a domain is a granular attribution function.

Every surmise function on a domain is a granular attribution function.

Proof 
                         Let  
                               σ 
                             be a surmise function on a domain  
                               Q 
                            . By  Lemma 13 (2),  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        σ 
                                     
                                     
                                        ⋇ 
                                     
                                  
                                  ≈ 
                                  σ 
                               
                            . It follows from  Lemma 12  that  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        
                                           
                                              σ 
                                           
                                           
                                              ⋇ 
                                           
                                        
                                     
                                     
                                        ̂ 
                                     
                                  
                                  ≈ 
                                  
                                     
                                        σ 
                                     
                                     
                                        ̂ 
                                     
                                  
                               
                            . Furthermore,  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        σ 
                                     
                                     
                                        ̂ 
                                     
                                  
                                  = 
                                  σ 
                               
                             from  Lemma 13 (1). Also, it is showed that  
                               
                                  σ 
                                  ≾ 
                                  
                                     
                                        σ 
                                     
                                     
                                        ⋇ 
                                     
                                  
                               
                             in the proof of  Proposition 2 . Consequently,  
                               
                                  
                                     
                                        
                                           
                                              σ 
                                           
                                           
                                              ⋇ 
                                           
                                        
                                     
                                     
                                        ̂ 
                                     
                                  
                                  ≾ 
                                  
                                     
                                        σ 
                                     
                                     
                                        ⋇

                                     σ 
                                  
                                  
                                     ⋇ 
                                  
                               
                             has a reduct. By  Theorem 3 ,  
                               σ 
                             is granular. □

Example 2  shows that  Proposition 8  cannot be reverted. In fact, let  
                         σ 
                       be the attribution function described in  Example 2 . Then  
                         σ 
                       is a granular attribution function. However,  
                         
                            Q 
                            ∈ 
                            σ 
                            
                               ( 
                               1 
                               ) 
                            
                         
                      ,  
                         
                            Q 
                            ∖ 
                            
                               { 
                               2 
                               } 
                            
                            ∈ 
                            σ 
                            
                               ( 
                               1 
                               ) 
                            
                         
                       and  
                         
                            Q 
                            ∖ 
                            
                               { 
                               2 
                               } 
                            
                            ⊂ 
                            Q 
                         
                      . It shows that  
                         σ 
                       does not satisfy  Definition 2 (3) for  
                         
                            q 
                            = 
                            1 
                         
                      . So  
                         σ 
                       is not a surmise function.

In this paper, we introduce the completeness and the completion for attribution functions. Further, we give a general way to derive a attribution function from a knowledge structure on an arbitrary domain. With the help of this derivation, we introduce the notion of a dual attribution function and obtain that the completion of an attribution function equals its dual attribution function. Based on this, we establish a Galois connection as follows.

Let  
                         K 
                       be the collection of all knowledge structures on an arbitrary domain  
                         Q 
                       and  
                         F 
                       the collection of all attribution functions on  
                         Q 
                      . Additionally, let  
                         ⊆ 
                       and  
                         ≾ 
                       be the relation of set inclusion and the quasi order on  
                         F 
                       introduced in  Definition 2 , respectively. We establish a Galois connection between  
                         
                            ( 
                            K 
                            , 
                            ⊆ 
                            ) 
                         
                       and  
                         
                            ( 
                            F 
                            , 
                            ≾ 
                            ) 
                         
                      . Here, the closed elements of this Galois connection in  
                         K 
                       are the knowledge spaces, and in  
                         F 
                       are the complete attribution functions. Moreover, this Galois connection induces a one-to-one correspondence between the two sets of closed elements.

As another interesting result, we introduce the reduct of attribution functions to prove that an attribution function is granular if and only if its completion has a reduct, which gives an answer to an open problem on the granularity of attribution functions posed by Falmagne and Doignon (i.e., Open Problem 18.3.2 in  Falmagne & Doignon, 2011 ). Specially, a complete attribution function is granular if and only if it has a reduct.

The authors would like to express their gratitude to Professor Jürgen Heller and the Reviewer for their thoughtful comments and detailed suggestions. In particular, the authors thank Professor Jürgen Heller for providing the concrete frameworks of establishing the Galois connection.
